<br />
<br />This section covers the use of the updated java.nio package to read and write files. In particular, it shows how the power of Java 8 Streams to simplify reading files and exploring folders. See http:&#x2F;&#x2F;www.coreservlets.com&#x2F;java-8-tutorial&#x2F; for the complete tutorial, downloadable and printable PDF files, source code, exercises, and exercise solutions.

    Topics in This Section
&#x2022; More on try/catch blocks
&#x2013; finally, multicatch, try-with-resources

&#x2013; Paths.get
&#x2022; Reading files

&#x2022; Writing files

  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-4-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 4 image" target="_blank">
        4.
      </a>
    &#xA9; 2015 Marty Hall
Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/
Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Android, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring MVC, RESTful Web Services, GWT, Hadoop.
Developed and taught by well-known author and developer. At public venues or onsite at your location.
More on try/catch
Blocks
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-5-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 5 image" target="_blank">
        5.
      </a>
    Summary
&#x2022; Covered earlier:
basics
try {
statement1;
statement2;
...
} catch(Eclass1 var1) {
...
} catch(Eclass2 var2) {
...
} catch(Eclass3 var3) {
...
}
&#x2026;
&#x2022; New: finally
try {&#x2026;
} catch(&#x2026;) {&#x2026;
} finally {
&#x2026;
}
&#x2022; New: multicatch
try {&#x2026;
} catch(Eclass1 | Eclass e) {
&#x2026;
} &#x2026;
&#x2022; New: try with resources
try (SomeAutoCloseable var = &#x2026;) {&#x2026;
} catch(&#x2026;) { &#x2026;
} &#x2026;
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-6-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 6 image" target="_blank">
        6.
      </a>
    Finally Blocks
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; The finally { &#x2026; } block at the end of a try/catch is called
whether or not there is an exception
&#x2022; Motivation: resetting resources
HugeDataStructure blah = &#x2026;;
try {
doSomethingWith(blah);
&#x2026;
} catch {
&#x2026;
} finally {
blah = null;
}
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-7-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 7 image" target="_blank">
        7.
      </a>
    Finally Blocks: Benefits
&#x2022; Question: difference between these two?
&#x2022; Answer: nested try/catch blocks
&#x2013; In the example on the right above, if the catch throws an
exception and the entire try/catch block is inside another
try/catch block, the cleanup code might not run.
&#x2022; So, usual practice for code that runs whether or not there
is an exception is to simply put it below try/catch block (as
in example on right above), but finally block is sometimes
necessary.
Finally Block Code After Entire try/catch
try { &#x2026;
} catch(&#x2026;) { &#x2026;
} finally {
doSomeCleanup();
}
try { &#x2026;
} catch(&#x2026;) { &#x2026;
}
doSomeCleanup();
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-8-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 8 image" target="_blank">
        8.
      </a>
    Multicatch
&#x2022; Idea: can catch multiple exceptions using |
&#x2013; In Java 7 and later, if two different catch blocks will do
the same thing, you can catch more than one in the same
catch clause (but also consider catching a parent type):
&#x2022; try { &#x2026; } catch(Eclass1 | Eclass2 e) {&#x2026;}
&#x2022; Example
Without Multicatch With Multicatch
String strng = getSomeString();
int num;
try {
num = Integer.parseInt(strng);
} catch(NumberFormatException nfe) {
num = someDefault;
} catch(NullPointerException npe) {
num = someDefault;
}
String strng = getSomeString();
int num;
try {
num = Integer.parseInt(strng);
} catch(NumberFormatException | NullPointerException e) {
num = someDefault;
}
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-9-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 9 image" target="_blank">
        9.
      </a>
    try-with-resources: Overview
&#x2022; Idea
&#x2013; In Java 7 and later, you can declare variables that
implement AutoCloseable in parens after try.
&#x2022; Scope of variable is scope of try/catch block
&#x2022; The close method of each variable is called at the end,
whether or not there is an exception (i.e., as if the call to
close were in a finally block)
&#x2022; Can declare multiple variables, separated by semicolon
&#x2022; Example
try (BufferedReader reader = &#x2026;) {
readSomeDataWith(reader);
&#x2026;
} catch(&#x2026;) {
&#x2026;
}
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-10-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 10 image" target="_blank">
        10.
      </a>
    try-with-resources: Benefits
&#x2022; Advantages of approach on right
&#x2013; Shorter and simpler
&#x2013; Can&#x2019;t forget to call close
&#x2013; The reader variable is out of scope after the try/catch
block finishes
Without With
BufferedReader reader;
try {
reader = &#x2026;;
&#x2026;
} catch (&#x2026;) {
&#x2026;
} finally {
reader.close();
}
try(BufferedReader reader = &#x2026;) {
&#x2026;
} catch (&#x2026;) {
&#x2026;
}
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-11-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 11 image" target="_blank">
        11.
      </a>
    &#xA9; 2015 Marty Hall
Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/
Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Android, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring MVC, RESTful Web Services, GWT, Hadoop.
Developed and taught by well-known author and developer. At public venues or onsite at your location.
Paths
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-12-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 12 image" target="_blank">
        12.
      </a>
    Idea
&#x2022; Path is flexible replacement for File
&#x2013; And is main starting point for file IO operations
&#x2022; Get Path with Paths.get
&#x2013; Path p1 = Paths.get("some-file");
&#x2013; Path p2 = Paths.get("/usr/local/gosling/some-file");
&#x2013; Path p3 =
Paths.get("C:UsersGoslingDocumentssome-file");
&#x2022; Notice the double backslashes because backslash already
has meaning (escape next char) in Java strings.
&#x2022; Paths have convenient methods
&#x2013; toAbsolutePath, startsWith, endsWith, getFileName,
getName, getNameCount, subpath, getParent, getRoot,
normalize, relativize
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-13-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 13 image" target="_blank">
        13.
      </a>
    Example
public class PathExamples {
public static void main(String[] args) {
Path p1 = Paths.get("InputFile.txt");
System.out.println("Simple Path");
System.out.printf("toString: %s%n%n", p1);
Path p2 = p1.toAbsolutePath();
System.out.println("Absolute Path");
System.out.printf("toString: %s%n", p2);
System.out.printf("getFileName: %s%n", p2.getFileName());
System.out.printf("getName(0): %s%n", p2.getName(0));
System.out.printf("getNameCount: %d%n", p2.getNameCount());
System.out.printf("subpath(0,2): %s%n", p2.subpath(0,2));
System.out.printf("getParent: %s%n", p2.getParent());
System.out.printf("getRoot: %s%n", p2.getRoot());
}
}
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-14-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 14 image" target="_blank">
        14.
      </a>
    Example Output
Simple Path
toString: InputFile.txt
Absolute Path
toString: C:eclipse-workspacejavanioInputFile.txt
getFileName: InputFile.txt
getName(0): eclipse-workspace
getNameCount: 4
subpath(0,2): eclipse-workspacejava
getParent: C:eclipse-workspacejavanio
getRoot: C:
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-15-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 15 image" target="_blank">
        15.
      </a>
    &#xA9; 2015 Marty Hall
Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/
Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Android, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring MVC, RESTful Web Services, GWT, Hadoop.
Developed and taught by well-known author and developer. At public venues or onsite at your location.
Simple File Reading
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-16-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 16 image" target="_blank">
        16.
      </a>
    Idea
&#x2022; You can read all lines into Stream in 1 method call
&#x2013; Stream&lt;String&gt; lines = Files.lines(somePath);
&#x2022; Quick example
&#x2013; Given large file of words of various lengths in mixed case with
possible repeats, create sorted uppercase file of n-letter words
List&lt;String&gt; words =
Files.lines(Paths.get(inputFileName))
.filter(s -&gt; s.length() == n)
.map(String::toUpperCase)
.distinct()
.sorted()
.collect(Collectors.toList());
Files.write(Paths.get(outputFileName), words, Charset.defaultCharset());
This code is slightly over-simplified:
&#x2022; You need to catch IOException
&#x2022; You should close the Stream that results from Files.lines
so that long-running code will not have memory leak.
Still, this gives the gist of the approach. Full code for this
task (using try-with-resources) is given later in this tutorial
section.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-17-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 17 image" target="_blank">
        17.
      </a>
    Benefits
&#x2022; Java 7 already let you read all lines into List
&#x2013; List&lt;String&gt; lines =
Files.readAllLines(somePath, someCharset);
&#x2022; But Stream version far better
&#x2013; Massive memory savings
&#x2022; Does not store entire file contents in one huge list, but
processes each line as you go along
&#x2013; Potentially much faster
&#x2022; You can stop partway through, and rest of file is never
processed (due to lazy evaluation of Streams)
&#x2013; Many convenient filtering and transformation methods
&#x2022; You can chain these method calls together
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-18-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 18 image" target="_blank">
        18.
      </a>
    Files.lines: More Details
&#x2022; Charset option
&#x2013; Files.lines(path)
&#x2022; Uses UTF-8
&#x2013; Files.lines(path, someCharset)
&#x2022; Uses specified Charset
&#x2022; Throws IOException
&#x2013; So must use try/catch block
&#x2022; Stream should be closed
&#x2013; Most Streams do not need closing, but ones connected to
IO sources (as here) do.
&#x2022; Stream implements AutoCloseable
&#x2013; You can handle IOException and automatically call
close() via try-with-resources
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-19-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 19 image" target="_blank">
        19.
      </a>
    Files.lines: Usage Template
public SomeType useStream(Stream&lt;String&gt; lines, ...) {
return(lines.filter(&#x2026;).map(&#x2026;)&#x2026;);
}
public SomeType useFile(String filename, ...) {
try(Stream&lt;String&gt; lines =
Files.lines(Paths.get(filename))) {
return(useStream(lines, ...));
} catch(IOException ioe) {
System.err.println("IOException: " + ioe);
return(null);
}
}
It is better to put the processing of the Stream&lt;String&gt; in another method, not in the same method as you call Files.lines.
&#x2022; You simplify testing. You can test the other method with a basic Stream that you make with Stream.of or someList.stream().
&#x2022; It is more reusable. The other method can be used for Streams created from other sources.
&#x2022; It is more flexible. The other method can take a Stream&lt;T&gt;, where T is a generic type, and thus can be used for a variety of
purposes, not just String processing.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-20-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 20 image" target="_blank">

    Finding First Fancy Palindrome:
String-Specific Version
public static String firstPalindrome(Stream&lt;String&gt; words,
int n, String substring) {
return(words.filter(word -&gt; word.length() == n)
.filter(word -&gt; word.contains(substring))
.filter(StringUtils::isPalindrome)
.findFirst()
.orElse(null));
}
public static String firstPalindrome(String filename,
int n, String substring) {
try(Stream&lt;String&gt; words =
Files.lines(Paths.get(filename))) {
return(firstPalindrome(words, n, substring));
} catch(IOException ioe) {
System.err.println("IOException: " + ioe);
return(null);
}
Finds first n-letter palindrome that
contains the specified substring.

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-27-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 27 image" target="_blank">
        27.
      </a>
    Generic Helper Methods:
Finding Matches
@SafeVarargs
public static &lt;T&gt; Predicate&lt;T&gt; combinedPredicate
(Predicate&lt;T&gt;... tests) {
Predicate&lt;T&gt; result = e -&gt; true;
for(Predicate&lt;T&gt; test: tests) {
result = result.and(test);
}
return(result);
}
@SafeVarargs
public static &lt;T&gt; T firstMatch(Stream&lt;T&gt; elements,
Predicate&lt;T&gt;... tests) {
Predicate&lt;T&gt; combinedTest = combinedPredicate(tests);
return(elements.filter(combinedTest)
.findFirst()
.orElse(null));
}
Returns a Predicate that is the result of ANDing all
the argument Predicates. If no Predicates are
supplied, it returns a Predicate that always
returns true.
Returns first element that matches all of the tests,
null otherwise.
@SafeVarargs is difficult to understand. The issue is that it is not always safe to use varargs for generic types: the resultant array can have runtime type problems if you modify entries in it. @SafeVarargs
says &#x201C;I am not doing anything dangerous, please suppress the compiler warnings&#x201D;. For details, see http://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/technotes/guides/language/non-reifiable-varargs.html
 
  </li>

      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-28-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 28 image" target="_blank">

    Finding Total Number of Chars
of Words Passing Tests
public static int letterCount(Stream&lt;String&gt; words,
Predicate&lt;String&gt; test) {
return(words.filter(test)
.mapToInt(String::length)
.sum());
}
public static int letterCount(String filename,
Predicate&lt;String&gt; test) {
try(Stream&lt;String&gt; words =
Files.lines(Paths.get(filename))) {
return(letterCount(words, test));
} catch(IOException ioe) {
System.err.println("IOException: " + ioe);
return(0);
}
}
The sum of the lengths of all words
that pass the test.

public static void letterCountExamples(String filename) {
printLetterCountResult(filename, StringUtils::isPalindrome,
"are palindromes");
Predicate&lt;String&gt; containsQ = s -&gt; s.contains("q");
printLetterCountResult(filename, containsQ, "contain q");
Predicate&lt;String&gt; containsQButNotU =
containsQ.and(s -&gt; !s.contains("u"));
printLetterCountResult(filename, containsQButNotU,
"contain q but not u");
printLetterCountResult(filename, s -&gt; true, "are in file");
}

message, sum);
}

Simple File Writing
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-32-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 32 image" target="_blank">
        32.
      </a>
    Idea
&#x2022; You can write all lines in one method call
&#x2013; List&lt;String&gt; lines = &#x2026;;
&#x2022; Recall that you can turn Stream into List with
strm.collect(Collectors.toList()).
&#x2022; You can actually use any Iterable&lt;String&gt;, not just List&lt;String&gt;.
&#x2013; You would think you could also use List&lt;Object&gt; and the system would call the
toString method of each Object automatically. Sadly, no.
&#x2013; Files.write(somePath, lines, someCharset);
&#x2022; You can write all bytes in one method call
&#x2013; byte[] fileArray = &#x2026;;
&#x2013; Files.write(somePath, fileArray);
&#x2022; OpenOption
&#x2013; Both methods above optionally take an OpenOption as final
argument
&#x2022; This specifies whether to create file if it doesn&#x2019;t exist, whether to
append, and so forth. Default behavior is to create file if not there
and to overwrite if it is there.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-33-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 33 image" target="_blank">
        33.
      </a>
    Example 1: Write Strings to File
public class WriteFile1 {
public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException {
Charset characterSet = Charset.defaultCharset();
Path path = Paths.get("OutputFile1.txt");
List&lt;String&gt; lines =
Arrays.asList("Line One", "Line Two", "Final Line");
Files.write(path, lines, characterSet);
}
}

Final Line
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-34-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 34 image" target="_blank">
        34.
      </a>
    Example 2:
Store N-Letter Words
&#x2022; Task
&#x2013; Given large file of words of various lengths in mixed case
with possible repeats, create sorted uppercase file of n-
letter words.
&#x2022; Comments
&#x2013; File is large (1.5 million characters as shown in earlier
example), so storing entire file in memory in a List as
with the Java 7 Files.readAllLines described later would
waste memory.
&#x2013; The set of n-letter words for any n is much smaller, so
entire List can be stored in memory. Besides, since we
will sort the results alphabetically, we have little choice
but to store all the matches in memory.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-35-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 35 image" target="_blank">
        35.
      </a>
    N-Letter Words: Core Code
public static List&lt;String&gt; makeWordList(Stream&lt;String&gt; words,
int wordLength) {
return(words.filter(word -&gt; word.length() == wordLength)
.map(String::toUpperCase)
.distinct()
.sorted()
.collect(Collectors.toList()));
}
public static void storeWordList(String inputFile, int wordLength,
String outputFile) {
try(Stream&lt;String&gt; words = Files.lines(Paths.get(inputFile))) {
List&lt;String&gt; nLetterWords = makeWordList(words, wordLength);
Path outputPath = Paths.get(outputFile);
Files.write(outputPath, nLetterWords, Charset.defaultCharset());
System.out.printf("Wrote %s words to %s.%n", nLetterWords.size(),
outputPath.toAbsolutePath());
} catch(IOException ioe) {
System.err.println("IOException: " + ioe);
}
}
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-36-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 36 image" target="_blank">
        36.
      </a>
    N-Letter Words: Test Code
public static void wordListExamples(String inputFile) {
FileUtils.storeWordList(inputFile, 4,
"four-letter-words.txt");
FileUtils.storeWordList(inputFile, 5,
"five-letter-words.txt");
}

Exploring Folders
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-38-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 38 image" target="_blank">
        38.
      </a>
    Idea
&#x2022; Get all files in a folder
&#x2013; Files.list
&#x2022; Get all files in and below a folder
&#x2013; Files.walk
&#x2022; Get matching files in and below a folder
&#x2013; Files.find
&#x2022; With Files.walk above, you usually manually apply a
Predicate and only process certain files. Files.find
simplifies that: you also pass in a BiPredicate that takes a
Path and a BasicFileAttributes object, and Files.find
returns only the Paths that pass the test.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-39-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 39 image" target="_blank">
        39.
      </a>
    Example 1:
Printing Files in Folder
public class FolderUtils
public static void printAllPaths(Stream&lt;Path&gt; paths) {
paths.forEach(System.out::println);
}
public static void printAllPathsInFolder(String folder) {
try(Stream&lt;Path&gt; paths = Files.list(Paths.get(folder))) {
printAllPaths(paths);
} catch(IOException ioe) {
System.err.println("IOException: " + ioe);
}
}

public static void printAllPathsInTree(String rootFolder) {

} catch(IOException ioe) {

public static void printPathsInTree(String rootFolder,
Predicate&lt;Path&gt; test) {
try(Stream&lt;Path&gt; paths =
Files.walk(Paths.get(rootFolder))) {
printPaths(paths, test);
} catch(IOException ioe) {
System.err.println("IOException: " + ioe);
}
} Files.walk also has options where you can limit the depth of the tree searched and where
you can specify FileVisitOptions.
 
  </li>

      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-43-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 43 image" target="_blank">
        43.

FolderUtils.printAllPathsInTree(".");
System.out.println("Java files under project root");
FolderUtils.printPathsInTree(".",
p -&gt; p.toString().endsWith(".java"));
} All files under project root

      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-46-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 46 image" target="_blank">

    &#xA9; 2015 Marty Hall
Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/
Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Android, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring MVC, RESTful Web Services, GWT, Hadoop.

Faster and More
Flexible File Writing
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-47-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 47 image" target="_blank">
        47.
      </a>
    Idea
&#x2022; You often need to format Strings
&#x2013; Files.write does not let you format the Strings as you
insert them into the file
&#x2022; Need higher performance for very large files
&#x2013; Buffered writing writes in blocks, and is faster for very
large files.
&#x2022; Shortcut method for getting BufferedWriter
&#x2013; Files.newBufferedWriter(somePath, someCharset)
&#x2022; Can also use PrintWriter
&#x2013; Writer has only simple write method, but you can do new
PrintWriter(yourBufferedWriter), then use the print,
println, and especially printf methods of PrintWriter
&#x2022; printf covered in lecture on More Syntax and Utilities
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-48-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 48 image" target="_blank">
        48.
      </a>
    Example 1:
BufferedWriter Only
public class WriteFile2 {
public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException {
Charset characterSet = Charset.defaultCharset();
int numLines = 10;
Path path = Paths.get("OutputFile2.txt");
try (BufferedWriter writer =
Files.newBufferedWriter(path, characterSet)) {
for(int i=0; i&lt;numLines; i++) {
writer.write("Number is " + 100 * Math.random());
writer.newLine();
}
} catch (IOException ioe) {
System.err.printf("IOException: %s%n", ioe);
}
}
}
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-49-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 49 image" target="_blank">
        49.
      </a>
    Example Output

  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-50-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 50 image" target="_blank">
        50.
      </a>
    Example 2:
PrintWriter
public class WriteFile3 {
public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException {
Charset characterSet = Charset.defaultCharset();
int numLines = 10;
Path path = Paths.get("OutputFile3.txt");
try (PrintWriter out =
new PrintWriter(Files.newBufferedWriter(path,
characterSet))) {
for(int i=0; i&lt;numLines; i++) {
out.printf("Number is %5.2f%n", 100 * Math.random());
}
} catch (IOException ioe) {
System.err.printf("IOException: %s%n", ioe);
}
}
}
printf is covered in a separate tutorial section (More Syntax and Utilities). Even if you haven&#x2019;t seen that section
however, the usage here is moderately understandable: %5.2f is a placeholder where the number get
substituted in with 5 total spaces and 2 after the decimal point, and %n means a new line.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-51-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 51 image" target="_blank">
        51.

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-52-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 52 image" target="_blank">
        52.
      </a>
    &#xA9; 2015 Marty Hall
Customized Java EE Training: http://courses.coreservlets.com/
Java 7, Java 8, JSF 2, PrimeFaces, Android, JSP, Ajax, jQuery, Spring MVC, RESTful Web Services, GWT, Hadoop.
Developed and taught by well-known author and developer. At public venues or onsite at your location.
File IO in Java 7
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-53-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 53 image" target="_blank">
        53.
      </a>
    Differences from Java 8
&#x2022; Read lines into List instead of Stream
&#x2013; Files.readAllLines
&#x2022; Streams were not yet available in Java 7. Although
returning a List is much less convenient than the current
approach of returning a Stream, the Java 7 way was still
substantially better than the Java 6 way.
&#x2022; Need way of reading large files
&#x2013; Files.newBufferedReader
&#x2022; Since Lists do not support lazy evaluation like Streams do,
reading large files with Files.readAllLines is inefficient
because entire file contents is in memory all at once, and
because you read entire file even if the data you need is
near the top.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-54-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 54 image" target="_blank">
        54.
      </a>
    Simple File Reading in Java 7
&#x2022; You can read all lines into List in 1 method call
&#x2013; List&lt;String&gt; lines =
Files.readAllLines(somePath, someCharset);.
&#x2022; You can read all bytes in one method call
&#x2013; byte[] fileArray = Files.readAllBytes(file);
&#x2022; Strings can easily be made from byte arrays:
String fileData = new String(Files.readAllBytes(file));
&#x2022; Minor caveats
&#x2013; You have to explicitly specify a Charset, even if you will use
the default for the JDK
&#x2022; Charset cset1 = Charset.defaultCharset();
&#x2022; Charset cset2 = Charset.forName("UTF-8");
&#x2013; You still have to catch IOException
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-55-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 55 image" target="_blank">
        55.
      </a>
    File Reading: Example
public class ReadFile1 {
public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException {
String file = "InputFile.txt";
Charset characterSet = Charset.defaultCharset();
Path path = Paths.get(file);
List&lt;String&gt; lines =
Files.readAllLines(path, characterSet);
System.out.printf("Lines from %s: %s%n", file, lines);
}
}
printf is covered in a separate tutorial section (More Syntax and Utilities). Even if you haven&#x2019;t seen that section
however, the usage here is simple: %s is a placeholder where &#x201C;file&#x201D; and &#x201C;lines&#x201D; get substituted in, and %n means
a new line. You could replace the printf with this only-slightly-clumsier println version:
System.out.println("Lines from " + file + ": " + lines);
Either way, note that you can directly print a List (unlike an array), because List has a readable toString method.
The system will automatically put square brackets on the outside and separate entries with commas.
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-56-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 56 image" target="_blank">
        56.
      </a>
    File Reading: Example Output
&#x2022; Source of InputFile.txt
First line
Second line
Third line
Last line
&#x2022; Output of example code from previous slide
Lines from InputFile.txt:
[First line, Second line, Third line, Last line]
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-57-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 57 image" target="_blank">
        57.
      </a>
    Some Simple Java 7 Utilities
&#x2022; FileUtils.getLines("filename")
&#x2013; Reading file into a List&lt;String&gt;
&#x2022; FileUtils.writeLines("filename", list)
&#x2013; Writing file from a List&lt;String&gt;
public class FileUtils {
public static List&lt;String&gt; getLines(String file)
throws IOException {
Path path = Paths.get(file);
return(Files.readAllLines(path, Charset.defaultCharset()));
}
public static Path writeLines(String file, List&lt;String&gt; lines)
throws IOException {
Path path = Paths.get(file);
return(Files.write(path, lines, Charset.defaultCharset()));
}
}
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-58-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 58 image" target="_blank">
        58.
      </a>
    Minor Variation of ReadFile1
(Using Utility Method)
public class ReadFile1A {
public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException {
String file = "InputFile.txt";
List&lt;String&gt; lines = FileUtils.getLines(file);
System.out.printf("Lines from %s: %s%n", file, lines);
}
}
&#x2022; Output
&#x2013; Same as ReadFile1. E.g.:
Lines from InputFile.txt:
[First line, Second line, Third line, Last line]

  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-59-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 59 image" target="_blank">
        59.
      </a>
    Minor Variation of WriteFile1
public class WriteFile1A {
public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException {
List&lt;String&gt; lines =
Arrays.asList("Line One", "Line Two", "Final Line");
FileUtils.writeLines("OutputFile1.txt", lines);
}
}
&#x2022; Source of OutputFile1.txt after execution

Final Line
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-60-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 60 image" target="_blank">
        60.
      </a>
    Lower-Level but More Flexible
File Reading
&#x2022; You sometimes need only part of the file
&#x2013; Files.readAllLines reads everything, which is wasteful
&#x2022; Stores entire file in memory
&#x2022; No way to stop if you find the info you need early in file
&#x2022; Need higher performance for very large files
&#x2013; Buffered reading reads in blocks; faster for very large files
&#x2022; Shortcut method for getting BufferedReader
&#x2013; Files.newBufferedReader(somePath, someCharset)
&#x2022; BufferedReader has readLine method
&#x2013; Returns a String. Can chop the String into pieces using
StringTokenizer (weak but simple) or String.split (more
powerful but requires knowledge of regular expressions).
&#x2022; Details on parsing in lectures on network programming
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-61-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 61 image" target="_blank">
        61.
      </a>
    Files.newBufferedReader
Rarely Needed in Java 8
&#x2022; When Files.newBufferedReader beneficial
&#x2013; When you don&#x2019;t want to read full line at a time as String
&#x2022; E.g., if reading single characters or arrays of characters
&#x2022; Files.lines preferable most other times
&#x2013; Files.lines returns a Stream, and Streams use lazy
evaluation
&#x2022; Instead of entire file going into memory in advance as with
Files.readAllLines, each line is processed as you go along
&#x2022; You can quit partway through, so if you find the data you
need early on, you never have to read the rest of the file
&#x2013; As shown earlier, Streams have many convenient filtering
and transformation methods, whereas using
BufferedReader requires lower-level and less convenient
techniques
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-62-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 62 image" target="_blank">
        62.
      </a>
    Example
public class ReadFile2 {
public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException {
String file = "InputFile.txt";
Charset characterSet = Charset.defaultCharset();
Path path = Paths.get(file);
try(BufferedReader reader =
Files.newBufferedReader(path, characterSet)) {
System.out.printf("Lines from %s:%n", file);
String line;
while ((line = reader.readLine()) != null) {
System.out.println(line);
}
} catch (IOException ioe) {
System.err.printf("IOException: %s%n", ioe);
}
}
} This approach using Files.newBufferedReader would be useful in Java 7 if the input file was large, so that all the
lines are not stored in memory at once. In Java 8, you would just do Files.lines(path).forEach(System.out::println).
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-63-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 63 image" target="_blank">
        63.

      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-65-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 65 image" target="_blank">

    Summary: Try/Catch Blocks
&#x2022; finally blocks
try {&#x2026;
} catch(&#x2026;) {&#x2026;
} finally {
&#x2026;
}
&#x2022; multicatch
try {&#x2026;
} catch(Eclass1 | Eclass e) {
&#x2026;
} &#x2026;
&#x2022; try with resources
try (SomeAutoCloseable var = &#x2026;) {&#x2026;
} catch(&#x2026;) { &#x2026;
} &#x2026;
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-66-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 66 image" target="_blank">
        66.
      </a>
    Summary: File IO in Java 8
&#x2022; Use Path to refer to file location
&#x2013; Path somePath = Paths.get("/path/to/file.txt");
&#x2022; Read all lines into a Stream
&#x2013; Stream&lt;String&gt; lines = Files.lines(somePath);
&#x2022; Can now use filter, map, distinct, sorted, findFirst, etc.
&#x2022; You get benefits of lazy evaluation
&#x2022; Can output as List with collect(Collectors.toList())
&#x2022; Put Stream processing in separate method, and consider making version of
method that uses generic types
&#x2022; Write List or other Iterable into a file
&#x2013; Files.write(somePath, someList, someCharset);
&#x2022; Get Writer for more flexible output
&#x2013; Files.newBufferedWriter(somePath, someCharset)
&#x2022; Use write method, or wrap in PrintWriter and use printf
&#x2022; Explore and search folders and subfolders
&#x2013; Files.list, Files.walk, Files.find
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-67-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 67 image" target="_blank">
        67.
      </a>
    Summary: File IO in Java 7
&#x2022; Use Path to refer to file location
&#x2013; Path somePath = Paths.get("/path/to/file.txt");
&#x2022; Read all file lines into a List
&#x2013; List&lt;String&gt; lines =
Files.readAllLines(somePath, someCharset);
&#x2022; Write List or other Iterable into a file
&#x2013; Files.write(somePath, someList, someCharset);
&#x2022; Minor utilities shown (not builtin)
&#x2013; List&lt;String&gt; lines = FileUtils.getLines("filename");
&#x2013; FileUtils.writeLines("filename", someList);
&#x2022; Lower-level but more flexible readers &amp; writers
&#x2013; Files.newBufferedReader(somePath, someCharset)
&#x2022; To read, use readLine method
&#x2013; Files.newBufferedWriter(somePath, someCharset)
&#x2022; To write, use write method or wrap in PrintWriter and use printf
 
  </li>
  <li itemprop="text">
      <a href="http://image.slidesharecdn.com/08-file-io-nio-141222141347-conversion-gate01/95/file-io-in-java-8-applying-the-power-of-streams-68-638.jpg?cb=1425286439" title="View slide 68 image" target="_blank">
        68.

      slideshare_object.add_login_source('.j-favorite', 'slideview.top_toolbar.like');
      slideshare_object.add_login_source('.j-save', 'slideview.top_toolbar.download');
      slideshare_object.addSigninFrom('.j-favorite', 'favorite');
      slideshare_object.bindToModalLogin('.j-favorite');
      slideshare_object.bindToModalLogin('.j-save');

    slideshare_object.bind_favorites('#slideview-container');

    $(document).ready(function() {

      // Favorites update

      // Remove some sidebar list items to limit the sidebar's height
      var mainContentHeight = $("#main-panel").height();
      var sidePanelItemHeight = $("#side-panel .j-related-item").first().outerHeight();
      var numItemToDisplay = Math.floor((mainContentHeight - 200) / sidePanelItemHeight);

      $("#side-panel .tabs-content .content").each(function() {
        $(this).find(".j-related-item").slice(numItemToDisplay - 2).remove();
      });

        var loadAdditionalFunctionality = function() {
          e = document.createElement('script');
          e.type = 'text/javascript';
          e.async = true;
          e.src =  '//public.slidesharecdn.com/b/ss_foundation/combined_slideview_loggedout.js?5abab9f2a6d91d348b82837cd99ce2c685fef3b6';
          var s = document.getElementsByTagName('script')[0]; s.parentNode.insertBefore(e, s);
        };

        $(window).load(function() {
          loadAdditionalFunctionality();
        });


      // Load more atb when clicked
      $('.j-lazy-thumb-click').lazyload({
        event : 'more-tab-clicked'
      });

      $('.j-more-tab').on('click', function() {
        $('.j-lazy-thumb-click').trigger('more-tab-clicked');
      });

      // Load additionnal css
      $(window).load(function() {
        loadCSS("//public.slidesharecdn.com/b/ss_foundation/stylesheets/slideview.css?5abab9f2a6d91d348b82837cd99ce2c685fef3b6");
      });
    });
  </script>

  

  <noscript>
    <img height="1" width="1" alt="" style="display:none;"
      src="//www.bizographics.com/collect/?pid=870&fmt=gif" />
  </noscript>

  </body>
</html>
